### Post by shannon.soong on 2014-01-08
Hi - I'm new to Linux and am hoping someone can help save me.., well my HDD at least.  The data on my Seagate Central 3TB was no longer accessible in Windows, so I've opened the unit to retrieve the HDD and am trying to use Linux (Ubuntu 12.04 LTS) and a drive reader (via USB) to recover and copy the data off the drive.  The drive appears readible as all but the 'Data' partition seem to be able to mount.  However, when looking at the Disk utility, the Data volume will not mount.  I've been researching a number of help sites, and have tried a few things, but being new, am afraid to make the situation worse.

Here's are screenshots of the error that I receive when trying to mount the Data volume.  Let me know what additional info would be useful.  Any help is appreciated - thanks in advance!!

### Post by steeldriver on 2014-01-08
Hello and welcome to the forums

Your screenshot isn't showing for me - maybe you didn't upload it? (via the 'Manage Attachments' button in the 'Additional Options' box below the main text entry area)

Alternatively you can open a terminal window and enter

```
sudo parted -l
```

and copy + paste the output here

### Post by steeldriver on 2014-01-09
That all looks encouraging so far - for a little more information you can do

```
sudo lvs /dev/mapper/vg1-lv1
```
or
```
sudo lvdisplay /dev/mapper/vg1-lv1
```

or just go right ahead and try to mount it e.g.

```

sudo mkdir /mnt/seagate
sudo mount -t ext4 -o ro /dev/mapper/vg1-lv1 /mnt/seagate

```

---

### Post by steeldriver on 2014-01-16
Well the fact that the device was "no longer accessible to Windows" makes me think it's very possible the drive has either failed altogether or at least that the ext4 filesystem has become corrupted / unclean. Looking at the dmesg log *may* help to figure out what's wrong - but it may not. The next two things I would try would be (1) look at the SMART status of the drive (if it supports it) and run a filesystem check (e2fsck) on the LVM - but I don't want to advise you to do that since I don't have much experience of data recovery.

---

### Post by steeldriver on 2014-01-17
Doh! I have come across this before - I think it means the original hardware was Sparc-based, x86 systems generally have a 4k filesystem block size limit and are unable to mount filesystems with larger block sizes

A possible workaround using 'fuse' is described here --> [http://unix.stackexchange.com/questions/73536/how-can-i-mount-filesystems-with-4kb-block-sizes](http://unix.stackexchange.com/questions/73536/how-can-i-mount-filesystems-with-4kb-block-sizes)

---

### Post by steeldriver on 2014-01-19
Since the fuseexr2 command apparently executed without complaining (no error messages), the data should be available at ~/SG3tb - do you not see anything if you navigate there (i.e. to the directory named 'SG3tb' in your home directory)?

### Post by steeldriver on 2014-01-23
No I don't think so - it probably just means it mounted it belonging to root with permissions that don't allow ordinary users to access it. Try oening a new copy of the GUI file manager with admin privileges and using that - depending how your system is configured that will be either

```
gksudo nautilus
```
or
```
gksu nautilus
```

(may be *kdesu* if you're on a KDE-based desktop)
